< Text>
If you haven't had Ethiopian before, come here and let the kind staff recommend dishes based on your tastes. And for everyone who's familiar with the cuisine, you must visit Beteseb as soon as you can.

Come for the absolutely delicious food and genuinely warm service. Admittedly, I don't know much about Ethiopian food other than how much I love it. I ordered two beef dishes in addition to the veggie platter and was so pleased. We had two meat dishes with incredibly tender beef in a spiced stew that was intoxicatingly deep in flavor and aroma.

I will return to sample the entire menu.< /Text>

<username>Clara Chung<//username>< date>
1595824221772</date>
< Rate>
5<//Rate>
<Text>We got the doro wat and veggie combo to go. It was very good! Plenty of food for two people. The dishes were a little spicier than I'm used to for Ethiopian food, but no complaints here. I didn't think it was too spicy, but if you're sensitive you might disagree. The injera is 100% teff, which the owner was proud of--he should be! It was some of the tastiest injera I've had. Most places cut theirs with wheat, which doesn't taste as good to me. They gave us plenty of it, as well--we had enough for the meal.

I didn't see outdoor seating, but we came at the end of the day when they might have been winding down. In any case, they had space outside on a pretty wide sidewalk so I imagine they *can* have a couple tables out there. I noticed a few grocery type things like fresh whole spices; I'm hoping they start selling their berbere mix eventually.

The people running the place were very nice. Looks like a family--dad running the front, mom cooking in back, and I saw a younger woman as well. They mentioned they opened up just before the COVID lockdowns started happening--talk about bad timing! But I was happy to support their business and had a delicious dinner.< /Text>< pics>
None< /pics>

< Review>
This is one of the last places I went before all of the bars were shut down. On our way home from Monterey about a week ago, we stopped in for a couple drinks and games of pool. Nicole was bartending and it was really cool talking to her about her social life outside of the bar. Super intelligent and very friendly young woman!

I think it was the owner there also, Bubba I believe was the name, and he was just as fun and friendly. The people brave enough to be in the bar all got a drink of choice from him! Super nice to do, especially when you know business is going to be indefinitely shut down by the government.

The place itself was pretty cool. Darts, shuffleboard, TVs, lots of space... and just some of the nicest people there! That always is the best part of a bar for me. The social aspect is huge :)<//Review>

<Name>Alicia Strickland< /Name><Date>1564103308774</Date><rate>4</rate>< review>
My uncle has equipment here, so we went for a service call before the place was opened. So my review is for the establishment alone.

A pool table in the center. Juke box in the corner. Bar counter at the back. TVs above. I think there's even a dartboard. Black walls. I liked the look right away. The black walls are kind of stylish in an avant-garde kind of way. Sleek. Great atmosphere. If you'll pardon a feminine analogy, the black walls had a sort of little-black-dress chic-ness to them. (I might be a bit bias though. I'm trained as a decorator and have always wanted to try doing a room with black walls, giving them a little polish with some silver-leafing streaks or something...but I digress!)

I think the bartendress (that's a female bartender, for those who aren't sure) was named Deanna. (I may be wrong, and I apologize if I am, but it was something along that line.) Anyhow, she was super sweet, very talkative. I'd imagine she's a great bartendress as she seemed able to chat about anything. Very personable.

As I said, the bar wasn't open when I went, but I would imagine it's a nice place to hang out, shoot some pool (well, for those who do; I haven't quite mastered the game myself üòâ), and chat with friends. I'm told it's very popular, with a nice crowd till closing. Maybe one day I'll check it out during business hours. Since I'm always looking for new places to set a story (yeah, I'm a writer and about to get my first novel published--I know, I know. Shameless plug!), maybe I can set a scene there. üòÄ

Oh, about the four-out-of-five-stars rating: Since I didn't go while it was open, I didn't get the full effect of the place as a functioning bar, so I didn't give a full five.

Anyway, if pool and mingling are your thing, give Hideaway Lounge a shot.<//review>
